<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-800411987607289904 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=800411987607289904><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/161154369763409921/d760257b5ffd16af7a8fa7056574cc51.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong data-user-id=161154369763409921>kahnwong</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, January 17, 2021 2:11 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-800411987607289904>1/17/2021 2:11 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>1) notebooks cache variables, even when you&#39;re calling it outside its function --&gt; can cause an accidental major boop where &quot;wait where is this variable coming from&quot;
2) just because it&#39;s convenient to data scientists / analysts doesn&#39;t mean you can&#39;t make them export it to .py and make it work
3) more hoops to jump through just to get notebooks to be able to execute in prod
4) you can&#39;t use <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">git diff</code> with notebooks --&gt; code review, anyone?</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

But it carries some level of overhead. I.e. Either use databricks or the work to implement the delta connectors yourself. Definitely useful for streaming or higher velocity data sources. And you also get some optimization in databricks with respect to join performance. But it&#39;s certainly not a single solution for everything.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Maybe SD has some sort of distributed systems courses so that would be relevant too. 

Data science/analyst internships are scarce and most I imagine won&#39;t ask you to implement a system to programmatically collect the data as a project. DE internships are probably scarce too so I would just apply to a bunch of swe ones and ask during the late stages of the process about big data projects (especially if it&#39;s obviously a company that probably collects data).  Also, a lot of DE roles are posted as &quot;SWE (Data Team)&quot; so swe-&gt; DE is probably an easier pivot if you have trouble finding a job/internships initially. 

Maybe do a personal project in your free time or at a hackathon that pulls data daily from an api/other source, performs data quality checks, puts it into a DB, and then displays it on a web page using d3 or a tool like metabase. If you do happen to find a DE internship, maybe learn some SQL in addition to LC before it (but I&#39;d really hope most internships wouldn&#39;t expect sql since it&#39;s rarely taught. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-802608074207789056 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=802608074207789056><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/1.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rakkit.>rakkit.</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'802563788649922570')"> Before I make a fool of myself and they come back with &quot;we can&#39;t install updates because ##&quot;, are there any legitimate reasons that they wouldn&#39;t/couldn&#39;t? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=davemoedee data-user-id=222698391564451840>DaveMoeDee</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, January 23, 2021 3:37 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-802608074207789056>1/23/2021 3:37 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>There can be reasons one might not be able to update major SQL versions. Organizations can have internal software in maintenance mode that breaks if you move to a new version of SQL Server. I have seen this happen. There might also be a certification process needed before making any changes but the people who used to do that are no longer available. These are cases where companies are moving away from a product, but still have contracts to provide and support that product. This is a scary approach as they end up way behind on security updates. All of this is from the perspective of a SaaS business.

tldr; there can be process or staffing related reasons for not applying updates, and especially for not moving to new versions.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-802609253684609064 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=802609253684609064><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, January 23, 2021 3:42 PM">3:42 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I suppose there could also poorly written contract that lead to no updates. There can be contracts where customers can refuse to allow downtime to apply updates and 10 customers can share the same SQL instance. So long as a single customer refuses to allow an update, it could never happen. There would be no reason to not have transparency on this. 3+ years seems an implausibly long time though to not have any downtime.

If someone refuses to respond, you need to go up the ladder to get an explanation. Silos like that are unhealthy.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, January 23, 2021 3:43 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-802610235826896906 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=802610235826896906><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, January 23, 2021 3:46 PM">3:46 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Btw, if they come back with a reason for not installing updates, that doesn&#39;t make you sound like a fool. Communication of these things should be normal and accepted. Just don&#39;t email them, &quot;Dude, wtf? Why are no updates applied?&quot; Just tell them your problem and that the fix is in an update and ask if there is a reason why it can&#39;t be installed.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-803944190232625172 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=803944190232625172><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/97751494236848128/f8958b8da99b07774393c7c9e0fb3376.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/guilds/566333122615181327/users/195568875906138112/avatars/c3a5156a7632bc5c446e8f28d735696e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=.zeee>zee</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'803842829154910258')"> Hey all! I&#39;m looking into learning more about cloud products from a data engineer standpoint. Any advice on which platform to choose to learn? (GCP, AWS, Azure, etc) and what resource would be the best that&#39;s as close as real work? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=mashuma data-user-id=97751494236848128>jp</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, January 27, 2021 8:07 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-803944190232625172>1/27/2021 8:07 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Best resource to real world would be.. pick some unstructured data set, preferably rather dirty and use GCP, AWS to implement data pipeline. 

Basically try and solve some arbitrary business problem
1. Business has data
2. Make the data usable by the business

Something along the lines of 
<ul><li>Find data set (there are a ton available online)</li><li>Put it in cloud (e.g. s3) this will be your data lake / silo</li><li>Create pipelines to output the data in a RDBMS (e.g. aws redshift) star schema</li><li>Automate it</li><li>Produce analytical / insight dashboard 

Try to use the cloud offerings for this.

AFAIK AWS is vastly more popular, however while you should learn the cloud offering to <s>some</s> solid  degree, imho good data engineer is not locked in specific cloud vendor

My 2c</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, January 27, 2021 8:10 AM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>5</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

I&#39;ve been optimising our dashboard system for this use case recently and got medium analytics down from running 20 minutes to 1-2 minutes and for tiny datasets simpler queries run 2-10 seconds, but more complex ones really dont want to go below 30 seconds (simple NLP, calculating error margins, smoothing data with windows, imputation etc). we&#39;ll also have an external caching engine up soon enough so no same calculation has to be done twice, so waiting a minute on larger tasks isnt bad</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, January 29, 2021 5:53 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-804816272902062081 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=804816272902062081><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, January 29, 2021 5:52 PM">5:52 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;m on Spark 3.0 and use m5zn 2xlarge instances for this (fastest single core speeds). <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-807420331169808454 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=807420331169808454><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/475376346793508867/43b08a9e15b153a673e55d4566e9ec28.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=nick_o_rama data-user-id=475376346793508867>nick-o-rama</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, February 5, 2021 10:20 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-807420331169808454>2/5/2021 10:20 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>A job I did several years ago , we built a crawler that scraped hotel reviews off of popular review sites. I would spot check the data every now and then and noticed something was off. Sometimes the scraped reviews and review counts didn&#39;t line up at all. And repeated scrapings of the same hotel resulted in different reviews.

Turns out a popular review site had strange defense mechanism I&#39;ve never seen before or since. They didn&#39;t reject you, but instead served up <em>fake</em> reviews/ratings instead. It took me a bit to notice, and longer to figure out what exactly was happening.

We built in some more pauses and it didn&#39;t happen again.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=open_mouth><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=😮 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f62e.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div><div class=chatlog__reaction title=scream_cat><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=🙀 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f640.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-808794307103293501 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=808794307103293501><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/157149154663989248/0bfef2ef08a0d02d71b265af9f94661e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=eyian2656 data-user-id=157149154663989248>Eyian</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, February 9, 2021 5:19 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-808794307103293501>2/9/2021 5:19 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We started to use kinesis and if you go with java/Kotlin and Spring its pretty easy to use. But if you want to connect with Python or Spark Streaming it feels not really like an enterprise solution. I may be wrong since i am fresh in the streaming technology but there are some things that make me wondering: 

1. Checkpointing... if you use python you can use boto3 or KCL (which also use boto3). With boto3 you can do a lot but you have to do Checkpointing and a lot of stuff by urself. With KCL you get managed checkpointing but you are pretty limited to the options that kcl provides (again i just heard that from teammates). 

With Spark streaming if you want the same thing. you can use KCL but then ur gonna youe RDD or Structered straming then you have to do your checkpointing manually.

On the otherside with Kafka you dont have to worry about Checkpointing since that is included in the stream as i hear. 

2.  If there are no records inside a kinesis stream and you read it with  a python or spark consumer you will get permanently empty rows ... not a big dealbreaker ... still feels akward. 

This wont happens with kafka you only get whats inside a stream as i hear.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-808794632589672479 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=808794632589672479><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, February 9, 2021 5:21 PM">5:21 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>But <span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="divs.">@divya d</span> is right it is really easy to set up kinesis everything is managed by AWS i can imagine setting up kafka is more difficult, but i didnt done that yet.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I&#39;ve started hosting new projects on Siteground and have not had any issues.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

class SignatureMethod_RSA_SHA1(oauth.SignatureMethod):
    name = &#39;RSA-SHA1&#39;

    def signing_base(self, request, consumer, token):
        if not hasattr(request, &#39;normalized_url&#39;) or request.normalized_url is None:
            raise ValueError(&quot;Base URL for request is not set.&quot;)

        sig = (
            oauth.escape(request.method),
            oauth.escape(request.normalized_url),
            oauth.escape(request.get_normalized_parameters()),
        )

        key = &#39;%s&amp;&#39; % oauth.escape(consumer.secret)
        if token:
            key += oauth.escape(token.secret)
        raw = &#39;&amp;&#39;.join(sig)
        return key, raw

    def sign(self, request, consumer, token):

        key, raw = self.signing_base(request, consumer, token)

        # SSM support to fetch private key
        ssm_param = ssm.get_parameter(Name=&#39;jira_access_private_key&#39;, WithDecryption=True)
        jira_private_key_str = ssm_param[&#39;Parameter&#39;][&#39;Value&#39;]

        privateKeyString = jira_private_key_str.strip()

        privatekey = keyfactory.parsePrivateKey(privateKeyString)

        # Used encode() to convert to bytes
        signature = privatekey.hashAndSign(raw.encode())
        return base64.b64encode(signature)

But this is the line throwing the error
resp, content = client.request(request_token_url, &quot;POST&quot;)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

What I was trying to do: I was trying to read in a private key using tlslite.

It turns out that I wasn&#39;t storing my pem file the right way in system manager.

after adding -----------BEGIN PRIVATE KEY---------- and ----------END PRIVATE KEY-----------

I was able to read the file without issue</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<a href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/view-cap-theorem-practice-pavel-varyukhichev">https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/view-cap-theorem-practice-pavel-varyukhichev</a></span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class="chatlog__embed-color-pill chatlog__embed-color-pill--default"></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/view-cap-theorem-practice-pavel-varyukhichev><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">A view on the CAP theorem in practice</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Part 1. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-813536444626894888 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=813536444626894888><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/791013383179993089/2a9e48cbabb3eaaf4204c2db9595c79e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/195389093725601792/1c148cd15817cd1c5a87a2f9edfe6cf0.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=raxus2296>Raxus</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'813458422594797588')"> hey guys, I&#39;m a bit out of my depth here. I&#39;ve been asked to assess what we should use for the operational data store for our sub-50 ms query solution, and I&#39;m trying to pick between delta lake and dynamoDB, but I don&#39;t really understand what&#39;s going on. I&#39;m actually a machine learning guy who got stuck on a data engineering project, so I&#39;m a bit out of my depth?

I know the basics, dynamoDB is a noSQL db, and delta lake is a data lake type thing... but what that means in practice is out of my depth and I don&#39;t know what to google to figure it out. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rishabh_bhargava data-user-id=791013383179993089>rish</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, February 22, 2021 7:23 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-813536444626894888>2/22/2021 7:23 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Out of the two, DynamoDB is what you&#39;re looking for. For operational data store usage (which is low latency insert, update, delete), you need a transactional data store (either SQL-based like MySQL/PostgreSQL or No-SQL like DynamoDB or MongoDB). Delta Lake is more for analytical workloads where you&#39;re trying to do large aggregations or data science operations on large amounts of data.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-815676821890662401 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=815676821890662401><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/785221802754179164/5bc4e5c156304e6831c2ed63b7cba2e3.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=snidane8284>snidane</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'815653125783552040')"> clojure is interesting all by itself because it is lisp. It&#39;s good to know lisp. It&#39;s the purest high level programming you can imagine. However because of how powerful it is, it is not good for larger team because it allows for very easy customization of abstractions. Great for one, two person teams. Sad to say it, but for larger orgs you need dumber tools and follow standards.

Kotlin is &quot;Java done right&quot;. At least given recent advancements in programming languages. But I think many of these new cool features have made it to Java recently as well. I think of Kotlin as an interesting niche, but nothing which couldn&#39;t be done in Java these days. I might be horrinly wrong as I havent used it though. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=sspaeti data-user-id=785221802754179164>sspaeti</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, February 28, 2021 5:08 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-815676821890662401>2/28/2021 5:08 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>thanks again for your valid inputs! <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-815711933109895188 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=815711933109895188><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/469151026751209483/1cb6bb474129683a69282980c1522d6f.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=toxicafunk>toxicafunk</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'815694052422320158')"> static typing won the war, its just some ppl are still catching up to this fact </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=snidane8284 data-user-id=515302187031855114>snidane</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, February 28, 2021 7:28 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-815711933109895188>2/28/2021 7:28 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>No offence, but this is academics&#39; pipe dream.

Scala is on the way out and Haskell never even made it to the industry. Working with data, where lot of meaning is encoded within strings, requires ergonomics, not verbose useless static types. I am sure there is one great example where Haskell would excel, but working with 10 levels deeply nested JSON coming from an API you don&#39;t control isn&#39;t one.

Rust is a contender. Great for writing simple performant utilities. Do something more complicated and suffer when dealing with lifetimes and circular references.

Zig has potential to solve types in much better way - dynamically using comptime.

For data processing, composing structures in high level dynamic languages, which then compile to lower level tight loops in sql or tensor processors, is the way to go.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=eyes><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👀 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f440.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

It&#39;s an interesting progression and surely things will settle in the hybrid grounds somewhere. They won&#39;t ever go full static.

In python the new typing system is a nice documentation of functions at best. When I have a function receiving a df: pandas.DataFrame, the type wouldn&#39;t ever help me with understanding or validating of what&#39;s inside. &quot;df&quot; parameter name was enough of a hint to me that I should provide a dataframe.

I think the debate is actually settled for data processing field - it&#39;s mostly dynamic Python. Go is a nightmare for data processing. Tried working with jsons and almost puked.

I think more interesting debate is static/dynamic typing of data and not programming languages. Ie. schema-on-read vs schema-on-write</span></div></div></div></div></div>
